###SUMMARY: 
The patient is a 23-year-old male who presented to the emergency department with abdominal pain and nausea.
He has a history of hypertension, diabetes type 2, and obesity.
He was previously on medications such as metformin and lisinopril, but had not seen a primary care physician in a long time.
He also uses cannabis regularly.   
The patient's symptoms included nausea, vomiting, and abdominal pain, which improved with vomiting.
He also reported constipation, but his last bowel movement was the morning of admission.   
The patient's physical examination was notable for acute distress and upper abdominal tenderness to palpation with hypoactive bowel sounds.
Laboratory results showed a white blood cell count of 7.5 with 84% polymorphonuclear cells, hemoglobin of 13.5, and platelet count of 107.   
The patient underwent an endoscopy (EGD) which showed mild erythema in the antrum and moderate erythema and congestion in the stomach body.
Biopsies were taken.   
The patient's diagnosis was not acute intra-abdominal process, but rather diffuse anasarca, hepatic steatosis, and borderline enlarged spleen.   
At discharge, the patient was prescribed medications including Famotidine, Acetaminophen, and Haloperidol.

The patient underwent several surgeries, including an extended right colectomy, cholecystectomy, and ileostomy.
She also had a right hepatic laceration treated with argon beam coagulation and packing.
She was found to have extensive circumferential bowel wall thickening on CT scan, which was highly concerning for ischemic bowel.  
The patient's diagnosis was ischemic bowel, and she was also diagnosed with sepsis.
She was treated with antibiotics and pressor support, and her white count normalized.
She was discharged to a rehabilitation facility with a tracheostomy, gastrostomy, and ileostomy, and was instructed to follow up with her doctor and to resume her regular medications.  
The patient's medications at discharge included insulin, miconazole, lansoprazole, pregabalin, escitalopram, levothyroxine, metoprolol, and heparin.
